## `AcsCommitmentNoWaitCounterParticipantConfigStore`

- Introduced: `3.4.10`
- Deprecated: -
- Removed: -

Upstream docs: [Open](https://docs.digitalasset.com/operate/3.4/scaladoc/com/digitalasset/canton/participant/store/AcsCommitmentNoWaitCounterParticipantConfigStore.html)

**Signature**

```text
trait AcsCommitmentNoWaitCounterParticipantConfigStore extends AnyRef
```

**Summary**

get all active no wait configurations, with possibility to filter by synchronizers and participants. if no filter is applied all active no waits are returned.

- Deprecated: -
- Removed: -

**Signature**

```text
class AcsInspection extends AnyRef
```

**Summary**

Check that the ACS snapshot does not contain contracts that are still needed on the participant. In the context of party offboarding, we want to avoid purging contracts that are needed for other parties hosted on the participant.

<a id="type-com-digitalasset-canton-participant-store-activecontractstore"></a>

## `ActiveContractStore`

- Introduced: `3.4.10`
- Deprecated: -
- Removed: -

Upstream docs: [Open](https://docs.digitalasset.com/operate/3.4/scaladoc/com/digitalasset/canton/participant/store/ActiveContractStore.html)

**Signature**

```text
trait ActiveContractStore extends ActiveContractSnapshot with ConflictDetectionStore[LfContractId, Status]
```

**Summary**

The active contract store (ACS) stores for every contract ID whether it is ActiveContractStore.Active, ActiveContractStore.Archived, or ActiveContractStore.ReassignedAway, along with the timestamp of the latest change. Every change is associated with the timestamp and the optional repair counter of the operation (e.g. transaction, repair) that triggered the change. The changes are ordered first by timestamp, then by repair counter, and finally by change type (activations before deactivations). Implementations must be thread-safe. Updates must be idempotent.

<a id="type-com-digitalasset-canton-participant-store-contractandkeylookup"></a>

## `ContractAndKeyLookup`

- Introduced: `3.4.10`
- Deprecated: -
- Removed: -

Upstream docs: [Open](https://docs.digitalasset.com/operate/3.4/scaladoc/com/digitalasset/canton/participant/store/ContractAndKeyLookup.html)

**Signature**

```text
trait ContractAndKeyLookup extends ContractLookup
```

**Summary**

Find a contract with the given key. Typically used for Daml interpretation in Phase 3, where the key resolution is provided by the submitter. Returns scala.None$ if the key is not supposed to be resolved, e.g., during reinterpretation by Daml Engine. Returns scala.Some$(scala.None$) if no contract with the given key can be found.

**Members**

| Docs | Member | Introduced | Deprecated | Removed |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [Open](https://docs.digitalasset.com/operate/3.4/scaladoc/com/digitalasset/canton/participant/store/ContractAndKeyLookup.html#lookupKey(key:com.digitalasset.canton.protocol.LfGlobalKey)(implicittraceContext:com.digitalasset.canton.tracing.TraceContext):cats.data.OptionT[com.digitalasset.canton.lifecycle.FutureUnlessShutdown,Option[com.digitalasset.canton.protocol.LfContractId]]) | `lookupKey(key: LfGlobalKey)(traceContext: TraceContext): OptionT[FutureUnlessShutdown, Option[LfContractId]]` | `3.4.10` | - | - |
| [Open](https://docs.digitalasset.com/operate/3.4/scaladoc/com/digitalasset/canton/participant/store/ContractAndKeyLookup$.html#noContracts(namedLoggerFactory:com.digitalasset.canton.logging.NamedLoggerFactory):com.digitalasset.canton.participant.store.ContractAndKeyLookup) | `noContracts(namedLoggerFactory: NamedLoggerFactory): ContractAndKeyLookup` | `3.4.10` | - | - |

trait IncrementalCommitmentStore extends AnyRef

**Signature**

```text
trait ParticipantSettingsStore extends ParticipantSettingsLookup with AutoCloseable
```

**Summary**

Stores misc settings for a participant. Allows clients to read settings without accessing the database. In turn, a client needs to call refreshCache before reading settings.

**Signature**

```text
trait ReassignmentLookup extends AnyRef
```

**Summary**

Find utility to look for in-flight reassignments. Reassignments are ordered by the tuple (request timestamp, source synchronizer id), ie reassignments are ordered by request timestamps and ties are broken with lexicographic ordering on synchronizer ids.
